<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13559788023441605248">Welcome to the fabled Gold Coast, that stretch on the North Shore of Long Island that once held the greatest concentration of wealth and power in America. Here two men are destined for an explosive collision: John Sutter, Wall Street lawyer, holding fast to a fading aristocratic legacy; and Frank Bellarosa, the Mafia don who seizes his piece of the staid and unprepared Gol</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13559788023441605248">Welcome to the fabled Gold Coast, that stretch on the North Shore of Long Island that once held the greatest concentration of wealth and power in America. Here two men are destined for an explosive collision: John Sutter, Wall Street lawyer, holding fast to a fading aristocratic legacy; and Frank Bellarosa, the Mafia don who seizes his piece of the staid and unprepared Gold Coast like a latter-day barbarian chief and draws Sutter and his regally beautiful wife, Susan, into his violent world. Told from Sutter's sardonic and often hilarious point of view, and laced with sexual passion and suspense, The Gold Coast is Nelson DeMille's captivating story of friendship and seduction, love and betrayal.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13559788023441605248">...more</a>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This is one of my favourite books. It is brilliantly written, has an excellent story line and is witty to the point of laughing out loud all the way<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is one of my favourite books. It is brilliantly written, has an excellent story line and is witty to the point of laughing out loud all the way through (I first read this on the plane and was met with some strange looks). John Sutter has a hilarious sense of humour and all the characters work together with such ease. I loved it. Enjoy!<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_26487599">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26487599" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1302210-jessica" class="left imgcol" title="Jessica"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1219849534p2/1302210.jpg" alt="Jessica" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/26487599?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 06, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1302210-jessica" class="user" title="Jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast" title="Paperback 9780751531213" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26487599">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11136594839681154145">DeMilles best, and one of my all time favorite books - if you read nothing else by him, this is the one. Its awesome. Very clever and sarcastic, well researched, set on the <a title="The Gold Coast by Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast">gold coast</a> of long island with some mafia ties - I love love love this book and have read it like 6 times.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_11941106">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11941106" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/672073-diane-ehrlich" class="left imgcol" title="Diane Ehrlich"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Diane Ehrlich" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/11941106?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 07, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/672073-diane-ehrlich" class="user" title="Diane Ehrlich">Diane Ehrlich</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast" title="Paperback 9780751531213" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/672073-diane-ehrlich?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer11941106">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17194919804179785046">This is my all-time favorite from Nelson DeMille, one of my favorite writers. Although I like his writing for his characters, particularly his little-bit-of-a-smartass heroes and strong-willed, red-headed heroines (can't imagine why), his plots tend to be driven by international spy, military or police stuff. Not this one. Nice Long Island man has life ruined when Mafia don moves in next door. Funny, moving and beautifully written. I guarantee you will not be able to put it down. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_44345145">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44345145" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/927695-jessica" class="left imgcol" title="Jessica"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1203559718p2/927695.jpg" alt="Jessica" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/44345145?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 25, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/927695-jessica" class="user" title="Jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast" title="Paperback 9780751531213" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer44345145">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11631610906422359689">John Sutter is a lawyer living off of his wife's family fortune on the <a title="The Gold Coast by Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast">Gold Coast</a> of Long Island. These people and their friends are snobs. John is a pompous ass who is going through a mid life crisis. He needs an adventure, a challenge. And lucky for him, this challenge moves in right next door in the form of the boss of the NY mafia. The two become aquaintances, friends, business partners, lawyer/client, rivals... <br /><br />The relationship between these two men, as well as their wives is sleazy, but pr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11631610906422359689">John Sutter is a lawyer living off of his wife's family fortune on the <a title="The Gold Coast by Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast">Gold Coast</a> of Long Island. These people and their friends are snobs. John is a pompous ass who is going through a mid life crisis. He needs an adventure, a challenge. And lucky for him, this challenge moves in right next door in the form of the boss of the NY mafia. The two become aquaintances, friends, business partners, lawyer/client, rivals... <br /><br />The relationship between these two men, as well as their wives is sleazy, but predictable. None of the characters are likeable or relatable. This book could have used a better editor, as it was at least 200 pages too long. The story itself was dull and uneventful. I kept waiting for something to happen, and nothing really did. I've enjoyed reading Nelson DeMille in the past, but this was a big let-down. He portrays Long Island and Long Islanders well, but beyond that, the book was lacking.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11631610906422359689">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/58507-tara" class="user" title="Tara">Tara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/58507-tara?shelf=fiction-read" class="actionLinkLite">fiction-read</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer186290507">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17986607936971175521">So disappointing. Maybe a book so hyped is bound to fall flat. But John Sutter is without doubt one of the most annoying characters of any book I've read. <br /><br />His humor got easily tiresome. I couldn't stand one more "capisce" or "mamma mia." (I'm Italian, my family comes from Brooklyn, and not even with 50 of us in one room during the holidays do I hear that many "capisce" and never "mamma mia.") One day Sutter is a Gold Coast snob (I'm from Long Island and his type and his wife's type really exist)</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17986607936971175521">So disappointing. Maybe a book so hyped is bound to fall flat. But John Sutter is without doubt one of the most annoying characters of any book I've read. <br /><br />His humor got easily tiresome. I couldn't stand one more "capisce" or "mamma mia." (I'm Italian, my family comes from Brooklyn, and not even with 50 of us in one room during the holidays do I hear that many "capisce" and never "mamma mia.") One day Sutter is a Gold Coast snob (I'm from Long Island and his type and his wife's type really exist) and the next he's waking up hungover on a lawn and hanging with the Mafia. Annoying perhaps is an understatement.<br /><br />I'm a huge fan of DeMille's and even had the pleasure of interviewing him many years ago. He's a great storyteller. But The Gold Coast did not live up to what so many said will be one of the best books I'll ever read.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer37013287">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1353020481692363704">A very good story about the clash between a 40 year old lawyer on the North SHore of Long Island, his heiress wife and their dealings with a mobster. I found the story a little unbelievable. The Main character John Sutter mouth some really trenchant commentary about the North Shore, but I just did not really buy into the idea that even though he is inherently unhappy with his parents, and his wife's parents and sometimes with his wife and his safe life that he would just get so involved with the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1353020481692363704">A very good story about the clash between a 40 year old lawyer on the North SHore of Long Island, his heiress wife and their dealings with a mobster. I found the story a little unbelievable. The Main character John Sutter mouth some really trenchant commentary about the North Shore, but I just did not really buy into the idea that even though he is inherently unhappy with his parents, and his wife's parents and sometimes with his wife and his safe life that he would just get so involved with the mobster. Of course part of the reason he gets involved is that the mobster uses him.<br /><br />After seeing the Sopranos on television the impact of the mobsters is even more real. Anybody they touch is tarnished, and Sutter and his wife both are seduced and in some ways destroyed by both the <a title="The Gold Coast by Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast">Gold Coast</a> and their dealings with the mobster.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1340597484">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11991944905423743096">Nelson DeMille forwards this book with praises like it will change your life, the best book of all times and how readers have begged for the movie and I realized as I read the book the narrator John Sutter is doing the same through out the book to keep the readers from putting it down. Example the cynical sarcastic Sutter states I didn't know that later that day I'd be facing felony charges or Maybe what happened later wouldn't have happened if not for this event...etc... This novel is lauded as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11991944905423743096">Nelson DeMille forwards this book with praises like it will change your life, the best book of all times and how readers have begged for the movie and I realized as I read the book the narrator John Sutter is doing the same through out the book to keep the readers from putting it down. Example the cynical sarcastic Sutter states I didn't know that later that day I'd be facing felony charges or Maybe what happened later wouldn't have happened if not for this event...etc... This novel is lauded as the greatest since the Great Gatsby as it is the post generational look at the Gold Coast after Gatsby's death but where Gatsby had heart this has none. We have a cynical sarcastic narrator who marries a wealth cold cat-like woman with an over developed sexual appetite. Now John's ancestors are not the rich old money but working class which is already a problem for him as she owns everything and there's a prenup. As he is disillusioned with the society of blue bloods, snobs who are dishonest as the day is long, enter mafia boss Frank Bella Rosa a gangster right out of any novel with a mafia Don. Even his wife Anna is a cardboard cut out big breasted dumb and family orientated. The novel went into such great detail about the homes etc... and no one was the least bit likeable. But it did work to put me to sleep several nights. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11991944905423743096">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_149507093">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149507093" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3265660-mainon" class="left imgcol" title="Mainon"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1266350850p2/3265660.jpg" alt="Mainon" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/149507093?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 11, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3265660-mainon" class="user" title="Mainon">Mainon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast" title="Paperback 9780751531213" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mainon by: </span>
      Kevin Flatley
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3265660-mainon?shelf=kindle-books" class="actionLinkLite">kindle-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer149507093">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4868269763436459430">I kept comparing this in my head to Sidney Sheldon's <a title="Rage of Angels by Sidney Sheldon" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43328.Rage_of_Angels">Rage of Angels</a> -- both books are a few decades old, both involve lawyer main characters and Mafia-related secondary characters. I loved Rage of Angels, and really wanted to love this too. But I never quite *got* the marriage between John Sutter and his wife. We're constantly reminded that they love each other, but most of the time he doesn't seem to like her very much. Not that he dislikes her either -- he seems to feel curiously insouciant to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4868269763436459430">I kept comparing this in my head to Sidney Sheldon's <a title="Rage of Angels by Sidney Sheldon" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43328.Rage_of_Angels">Rage of Angels</a> -- both books are a few decades old, both involve lawyer main characters and Mafia-related secondary characters. I loved Rage of Angels, and really wanted to love this too. But I never quite *got* the marriage between John Sutter and his wife. We're constantly reminded that they love each other, but most of the time he doesn't seem to like her very much. Not that he dislikes her either -- he seems to feel curiously insouciant toward the beautiful, rich wife with whom he regularly has amazing and creative sex. The lack of emotion was weird and off-putting.<br /><br />The picture DeMille paints of the Gold Coast, however, was lovely and made me want to rent a car and drive out among the old mansions. <br /><br />There are a few recurring bits of the book that haven't aged so well; it seems silly that John has never heard of (and is horrified by the idea of) fried squid / calamari, and is overwhelmed by the discovery of Pellegrino, the fascinating Italian carbonated water. Also, at some point John makes a prediction that Little Italy will far outlast the Gold Coast because there's something so unchanging about it... but if you've been to Manhattan lately, you know Little Italy has shrunk to nothing but a two-block stretch of Mulberry Street.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4868269763436459430">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1012039752" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10979943-quillracer" class="left imgcol" title="Quillracer"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Quillracer" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1012039752?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10979943-quillracer" class="user" title="Quillracer">Quillracer</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1012039752">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17330433058599110133">I like Nelson DeMille. I’ve read close to a dozen of his books and liked them all until this one. I tried to stick it out to the end but gave up after slogging through 200 pages.<br /><br />The story plods along with nothing happening, just John and Susan Sutter, the main characters, ambling through their privileged lives. Everything happens at a pace more suitable to sweltering summer day.<br /><br />John and Susan are annoying and obnoxious. They act like spoiled kids and snipe at each other like siblings who hate ea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17330433058599110133">I like Nelson DeMille. I’ve read close to a dozen of his books and liked them all until this one. I tried to stick it out to the end but gave up after slogging through 200 pages.<br /><br />The story plods along with nothing happening, just John and Susan Sutter, the main characters, ambling through their privileged lives. Everything happens at a pace more suitable to sweltering summer day.<br /><br />John and Susan are annoying and obnoxious. They act like spoiled kids and snipe at each other like siblings who hate each other. John has no end of snarky comments about the people and homes of the Gold Coast while at the same time half-heartedly bemoaning the changes happening there. Susan is just bitchy. John, at least, displays a sense of right and wrong. Susan seems to function under the assumption that if she does it, it’s right. The antagonist, Frank Bellarosa is a caricature of a Mafia don.<br /><br />Everything that happens in the 600+ pages of <em>The Gold Coast</em>, DeMille covers in about 2 pages in <em>The Gate House</em>. That should give you an idea of how bloated this book is.<br /><br />Had I read <em>The Gold Coast</em> first, I never would have read <em>The Gate House</em>, the sequel and one of my favorite books. It caught and held my interest from the start. I can’t say that here.<br /><br />I may have to go back and re-read that book to get the bad taste of this dog out of my mouth.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17330433058599110133">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_77604807">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77604807" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/133202-erin" class="left imgcol" title="Erin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1294082070p2/133202.jpg" alt="Erin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/77604807?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 01, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/133202-erin" class="user" title="Erin">Erin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast" title="Paperback 9780751531213" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/133202-erin?shelf=book-club" class="actionLinkLite">book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer77604807">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9932298393417553751">I haven't read DeMille in a really long time (not since <a title="Plum Island by Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33810.Plum_Island">Plum Island</a> years ago) and I was grateful I had my Christmas break to get through it (sometimes a book comes just when you need to read it...I think I would've been frustrated by its 500 pages if I hadn't had long interrupted periods of time to read it). DeMille's style--sarcastic, biting, funny, honest--is on full display here.<br /><br />He takes a setting--the ultra rich in Long Island, from very old money--and explores it in a new, interesting insi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9932298393417553751">I haven't read DeMille in a really long time (not since <a title="Plum Island by Nelson DeMille" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33810.Plum_Island">Plum Island</a> years ago) and I was grateful I had my Christmas break to get through it (sometimes a book comes just when you need to read it...I think I would've been frustrated by its 500 pages if I hadn't had long interrupted periods of time to read it). DeMille's style--sarcastic, biting, funny, honest--is on full display here.<br /><br />He takes a setting--the ultra rich in Long Island, from very old money--and explores it in a new, interesting insider-y way. As I have not been, and never will be, super rich, I found it fascinating! John Sutter is a tax lawyer married to a very wealthy woman, who was given a huge piece of property by her parents (at 50 rooms it's so large they don't live there...they live in the guest house in the back). His life is predictable, but safe: grown happy children, a good sex life with his hot but slightly nutty wife Susan, a thriving practice, his boat, access to the upscale country clubs in their town, and of course, money (maybe it's not his, but it's money just the same). But the safety disappears as soon as notable mobster Frank Bellarosa buys the estate next door, seems to know John by name before they even meet, and eventually wants John to defend him in a murder rap.<br /><br />DeMille does a terrific job really showing how John gets sucked into the complex, dark world of Bellarosa's--there's an effective sense of foreboding and foreshadowing that things will NOT turn out well the closer John gets into Frank's world. The dialogue is crisp and snappy, and the characters are uniformly well-written...you may not agree with what John does or how he gets involved with Frank, but you can see why he does it. Frank Bellarosa simply challenges his masculinity, and tests John in a way that he must respond to. I also enjoyed how DeMille showed the complexities of the unconventional marriage between John and Susan, and it's ups and downs in a realistic way. Really sharp writing (although at page 400 I was ready for it to wrap up), and quite unique. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9932298393417553751">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3523778192812251407">Despite the logical errors- an upper crust couple is married at 20 and manages in that year to have a child, have the husband serve in the military AND become a lawyer? All this was pre-energy drink too!<br /><br />Despite the female lead being utterly unlikable-sorry, timeless beauty doth not a sympathetic person make<br /><br />Despite the Mafia thug being a mix of cunning and Disney-Frank Bellarossa leans on revisionist 'italian history' enough to make you think he took a taser to the head.<br /><br />Despite the MC being possi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3523778192812251407">Despite the logical errors- an upper crust couple is married at 20 and manages in that year to have a child, have the husband serve in the military AND become a lawyer? All this was pre-energy drink too!<br /><br />Despite the female lead being utterly unlikable-sorry, timeless beauty doth not a sympathetic person make<br /><br />Despite the Mafia thug being a mix of cunning and Disney-Frank Bellarossa leans on revisionist 'italian history' enough to make you think he took a taser to the head.<br /><br />Despite the MC being possibly the DUMBEST lawyer to ever pass the BAR-He asks his clients alibi five minutes before he's arrested? REALLY??<br /><br />Despite all this The Gold Coast is a riveting character study that works well in spite of the collection of heavily flawed and occasionally moronic characters. Ive read it several times and will likely read it several more. Unflinching in its structure, thankfully this story is utterly unmakeable into a motion picture and thus will be allowed to endure as is.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8737359274006215348">I've come to really enjoy Nelson DeMille's books. His main character here has a bit of the John Corey humor about him, but from a different mold. The story bogs down just a bit after the trial scene, but has a strong finish. The "over 40" crowd should be able to appreciate the whole mid-life crisis thing, too. All in all, I liked this book very much and can see why so many of DeMille's fan base wrote such great reviews for it.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_689216755">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689216755" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8478664-felicity" class="left imgcol" title="Felicity"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1381744619p2/8478664.jpg" alt="Felicity" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/689216755?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 16, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8478664-felicity" class="user" title="Felicity">Felicity</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/33813.The_Gold_Coast" title="Paperback 9780751531213" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer689216755">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10192487342749371775">This guy is such a witty, sarcastic genius I'm going to use a word I never use - it's awesome. Nelson DeMille is a master at bringing characters to life, and for me, this is ultimately what makes for a good novel. I feel like I know John and Susan Sutter personally and intimately, which is testament to the author's skill in character development and use of dialogue. DeMille admits to being asked many times (by women) if (a) he was John Sutter, and (b) if not, how could he be reached. Apparently</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10192487342749371775">This guy is such a witty, sarcastic genius I'm going to use a word I never use - it's awesome. Nelson DeMille is a master at bringing characters to life, and for me, this is ultimately what makes for a good novel. I feel like I know John and Susan Sutter personally and intimately, which is testament to the author's skill in character development and use of dialogue. DeMille admits to being asked many times (by women) if (a) he was John Sutter, and (b) if not, how could he be reached. Apparently the John Sutters of the world are not easy men to find. Susan, although being a challenge, seemed still to be worth the cost of her high maintenance. DeMille's success in getting the audience to like this complex personality despite her shortfalls, demonstrates yet again his superior literary skills.<br /><br />There will be more Nelson DeMille for me.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10192487342749371775">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15511314660743940995">Since we are right smack dab in the middle of summertime, I am going to recommend one of my favorite books OF ALL TIME. Yeah, I know DeMille is kind of a hack, but he was touched by the divine on this novel. I have read this book 10 times, and recommended it to over 40 people. Only one of them came back with anything but praise (and that dude was a Faulkner scholar at Duke, if that tells you anything ;).<br /><br />Let's just say the GREAT GATSBY meets THE GODFATHER. Wonderful stuff. And perfect for the bea</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15511314660743940995">Since we are right smack dab in the middle of summertime, I am going to recommend one of my favorite books OF ALL TIME. Yeah, I know DeMille is kind of a hack, but he was touched by the divine on this novel. I have read this book 10 times, and recommended it to over 40 people. Only one of them came back with anything but praise (and that dude was a Faulkner scholar at Duke, if that tells you anything ;).<br /><br />Let's just say the GREAT GATSBY meets THE GODFATHER. Wonderful stuff. And perfect for the beach or pool or anywhere. Great plot, compelling characters, wonderful setting, and a perfect sense of time.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16126713850907178561">As a new member of GoodReads, I'm just going back and retrofitting reviews for books that have impacted me over the years, whether good or bad. Gold Coast is in the former category. This was my first exposure to DeMille 15 or so years ago and more than his witty characters, I was blown away by his ability to embed social commentary on something like the Gold Coast way of life. It made me sad for a place I'd never even been. This book and Summerville are two that stand out that way for me.<br /><br />Unfortu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16126713850907178561">As a new member of GoodReads, I'm just going back and retrofitting reviews for books that have impacted me over the years, whether good or bad. Gold Coast is in the former category. This was my first exposure to DeMille 15 or so years ago and more than his witty characters, I was blown away by his ability to embed social commentary on something like the Gold Coast way of life. It made me sad for a place I'd never even been. This book and Summerville are two that stand out that way for me.<br /><br />Unfortunately, some of his later works lost much of that, but I will review those individually.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer446686807314649936">This was a very long book that never did pull me in all the way. Portions of it seemed to drag on. this surprised me as I have loved several others he has written. This book reminded me of the older prime time soaps which I could never get into either. I am currently reading another of his John Corey series, and I am enjoying it a lot.<br /><br />"Welcome to the fabled Gold Coast, that stretch on the North Shore of Long Island that once held the greatest concentration of wealth and power in America. Here tw</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText446686807314649936">This was a very long book that never did pull me in all the way. Portions of it seemed to drag on. this surprised me as I have loved several others he has written. This book reminded me of the older prime time soaps which I could never get into either. I am currently reading another of his John Corey series, and I am enjoying it a lot.<br /><br />"Welcome to the fabled Gold Coast, that stretch on the North Shore of Long Island that once held the greatest concentration of wealth and power in America. Here two men are destined for an explosive collision: John Sutter, Wall Street lawyer, holding fast to a fading aristocratic legacy; and Frank Bellarosa, the Mafia don who seizes his piece of the staid and unprepared Gold Coast like a latter-day barbarian chief and draws Sutter and his regally beautiful wife, Susan, into his violent world. Told from Sutter's sardonic and often hilarious point of view, and laced with sexual passion and suspense, THE GOLD COAST is Nelson DeMille's captivating story of friendship and seduction, love and betrayal." </span>

//&lt;![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uv4N5y/pX9EjSP0HCcnO8gIkvK3wLgCNOWi3nBB+y6PfKjI03TtLK6+Qibx3qChAS9N/tLnzRydTYbIO3Os95g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nFXf2+WQIXN3v8blxNNis5806tXuJAk/303m5Wf0qQT5geAIF0I1iftnsl66soQB1sMpzKf5TpW1RON3q2FfQQ==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

Good Enough to Dream is the&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText10025406729031280822\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Roger Kahn’s first major league hit was a grand slam: The Boys of Summer, his runaway bestseller that immortalized the 1950s Brooklyn Dodgers. Now Kahn does the same for players whose moment in the sun has not yet arrived. Good Enough to Dream is the story of his year as owner of the Class A, very minor league Utica Blue Sox. Most of the Blue Sox will never make it to the majors, but they all share the dream that links the small child in the sandlot with the bonus baby who has just smacked one out of the stadium. It’s a dream Kahn learned from his father and, in the course of a season, passes on to his daughter—hours of practice for a moment of poetry; a hard living but a touch of legend.\n\nGood Enough to Dream presents baseball unadorned, a game still sweet enough to lure grown men to leagues where first-class transportation is an old school bus and the infield is likely to be the consistency of thick soup. It is a funny and poignant story of one season and one special team that will make us hesitate before we ever call anything “bush league” again.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille">About Nelson DeMille</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille"><img alt="1238" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1377030719p2/1238.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer1074012223551615462">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille. He moved as a child with his family to Long Island. In high school, he played football and ran track.<br /><br />DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army and attended Officer Candidate School. He was a First Lieutenant in the United States Army (1966-69) and saw action as an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1074012223551615462">Nelson Richard DeMille was born in New York City on August 23, 1943 to Huron and Antonia (Panzera) DeMille. He moved as a child with his family to Long Island. In high school, he played football and ran track.<br /><br />DeMille spent three years at Hofstra University, then joined the Army and attended Officer Candidate School. He was a First Lieutenant in the United States Army (1966-69) and saw action as an infantry platoon leader with the First Cavalry Division in Vietnam. He was decorated with the Air Medal, Bronze Star, and the Vietnamese Cross of Gallantry.<br /><br />DeMille returned to the States and went back to Hofstra University where he received his degree in Political Science and History. He has three children, Lauren, Alexander, and James, and still lives on Long Island.<br /><br /> DeMille's earlier books were NYPD detective novels. His first major novel was By the Rivers of Babylon, published in 1978 and still in print, as are all his succeeding novels. He is a member of The Authors Guild, the Mystery Writers of America, and American Mensa. He was a past president of Mystery Writers of America and International Thriller Writers ThrillerMaster of the Year 2015. He holds three honorary doctorates: Doctor of Humane Letters from Hofstra University, Doctor of Literature from Long Island University, and Doctor of Humane Letters from Dowling College.<br /><br />Nelson DeMille is the author of: By the Rivers of Babylon, Cathedral, The Talbot Odyssey, Word of Honor, The Charm School, The Gold Coast, The General's Daughter, Spencerville, Plum Island, The Lion's Game, Up Country, Night Fall, Wild Fire, The Gate House, The Lion, The Panther, The Quest, and Radiant Angel. He also co-authored Mayday with Thomas Block and has contributed short stories, book reviews, and articles to magazines and newspapers. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1074012223551615462">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/1238.Nelson_DeMille" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Nelson DeMille...</a>

Now, ten years later, he has come home to the Gold Coast, that str&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText7965230008080848671\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;When John Sutter\'s aristocratic wife killed her mafia don lover, John left America and set out in his sailboat on a three-year journey around the world, eventually settling in London. Now, ten years later, he has come home to the Gold Coast, that stretch of land on the North Shore of Long Island that once held the greatest concentration of wealth and power in America, to attend the imminent funeral of an old family servant. Taking up temporary residence in the gatehouse of Stanhope Hall, John finds himself living only a quarter of a mile from Susan who has also returned to Long Island. But Susan isn\'t the only person from John\'s past who has reemerged: Though Frank Bellarosa, infamous Mafia don and Susan\'s ex-lover, is long dead, his son, Anthony, is alive and well, and intent on two missions: Drawing John back into the violent world of the Bellarosa family, and exacting revenge on his father\'s murderer--Susan Sutter. At the same time, John and Susan\'s mutual attraction resurfaces and old passions begin to reignite, and John finds himself pulled deeper into a familiar web of seduction and betrayal. In THE GATE HOUSE, acclaimed author Nelson Demille brings us back to that fabled spot on the North Shore -- a place where past, present, and future collides with often unexpected       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1603282-the-gold-coast">Quotes from The Gold Coast</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“What these people were trying to create or re-create here in this new world is beyond me. I can't put myself in their minds or their hearts, but I can sympathize with their struggle for an identity, with their puzzlement, which has troubled Americans from the very beginning - Who are we, where do we fit in, where are we going?”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/699709-what-these-people-were-trying-to-create-or-re-create-here" class="actionLinkLite">4 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“I wasn't sure about that, but one never knows.
